<div id="review_196386894" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/196386894" />
    <a title="Maria " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5769334-maria"><img alt="Maria " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600318539p2/5769334.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/196386894?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria " href="/user/show/5769334-maria">Maria </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer196386894" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1323331237249802538"><br/>What would you do if you have fallen in love with a man who only existed in your dreams? What if you found out that he was real but existed in a different time? What would you do to be with that person? What would you give to be with that person forever?<br/><br/><br/>Michele Winsor had a recurring dream. She had been having the same dream about a handsome blue-eyed man in a mirror and a skeleton key. She feels that she knows the person in the mirror but she couldn’t tell who it was, where they met or how she </span>
  <span id="freeText1323331237249802538" style="display:none"><br />What would you do if you have fallen in love with a man who only existed in your dreams? What if you found out that he was real but existed in a different time? What would you do to be with that person? What would you give to be with that person forever?<br /><br /><br />Michele Winsor had a recurring dream. She had been having the same dream about a handsome blue-eyed man in a mirror and a skeleton key. She feels that she knows the person in the mirror but she couldn’t tell who it was, where they met or how she knew him. As for the key, she doesn’t recognize it at all. But she was curious as to why she kept on getting the same dream but that wasn’t going to be answered until later in the book.<br /><br />Michele lived a simple life with her mother. She never knew who her father was because he left them when she was young and never returned. Still she was happy and contented even if they weren’t living the lifestyle of the rich and famous. <br /><br />Her life crumbled after the death of her mother Marion. She didn’t know how to move on because she was the only family she ever had. <br /><br />Now that her mother passed away her legal appointed guardians now were her grandparents who lived in New York. She was told that she had to leave her friends in California and move to New York to live with the Winsors. <br /><br />The Windsors were filthy rich. They were considered as one of the richest family in New York. Michele didn’t know how rich they really were until she arrived at the Winsor mansion which was too ostentatious for her taste. She preferred to be with her mother in their bungalow in California but she knew that wasn’t going to happen anymore.<br /><br />The Winsor mansion was not only huge and extravagant but it also holds her family’s history. At her room in the mansion, she found out that most of the Windsor girls actually stayed in her room even her mother. She was exploring her room when she came across a locked drawer. She didn’t have the key but she had an idea.<br /><br />Rummaging through her mother’s stuff she found a key. The same skeleton key she had seen in her dreams. She tried to use the key to open the locked drawer which miraculously opened the drawer.<br /><br />Inside the drawer was a diary. As she flipped through the first entry she was unexpectedly sucked inside the diary where she landed in her own bedroom back in 1901.<br /><br />As she goes back in time, she learns about her family and most of all she learns about who the man in the mirror is. <br /><br /><br />REVIEW: <br /><br />After reading “The Time Traveler’s Wife” I haven’t read any other books related to time travel. I loved the Time Traveler’s wife but reading it got me confused with all the jumping of time and stuff. With Timeless it was different; the flow of the book was fluid and continuous. It was not confusing since it was happening continuously. This book was narrated in the third person which I thought was great. Everything that was happening to Michele in the past and in the future was simultaneous so it won’t confuse you unlike in Time Traveler’s wife.<br /> <br /><br />The story started off with a dream which I really liked. <br /><br /><br />Michele Windsor was down to earth and very simple. I liked that. She was raised well by her mother because even if she knew that she belonged to a rich family that didn’t get to her. She was a very likeable character. She falls in love with Philip. She continues to travel back in time not only to be with him but also to help the Windsor girls with their issues. She learned that what she does in the past definitely affects the future so she made every action and moment count.<br /><br />Philip Walker was the man in the mirror. He was the blue eyed guy that Michele has been dreaming of. He fell in love with Michele even though he knew that she was from the future. He was a musician which drew me to him. He was everything that a perfect gentleman should be. (You would see why I said so). He kept his promise and that made me so happy by the end of the book I was still crying. I thought he wouldn’t be able to do it but he did! :)<br /><br />Marion Windsor was a cool mom. She kind of reminds me of myself. I am a single mom and I know how hard it is to raise a child all on your own. She did a pretty good job in raising Michele. She didn’t go back to her parents after Henry left. She continued to live the life she chose even if the love of her life left her alone leaving her with a key and their daughter.<br /><br />Dorothy and Walter Windsor were Michele’s grandparents. I think they were definitely keeping something from Michele regarding her father. Michele somehow has a clue because of what happened when she was in the past but still I think there was something else that they were hiding.<br /><br />Caissie Walker was a good friend. I mean its not every day that you meet someone who would believe you if you say that you could travel back in time. <br /><br />This book was the first in the series so you should expect that the ending was a bit of a cliffhanger but in a good way. I didn’t expect how it ended to tell you honestly.<br /><br />I was in tears as I was nearing the end of the book. I thought that it was not going to have a happy ending. Boy was I so surprised! I won’t go into details on that because that part would ruin everything. The ending for me was the highlight of the book. <br /><br />Love knows no boundaries. Love knows no time. Love knows no obstacles. To be with the person they love they would do anything or everything they could to be with that person. No one or nothing could ever tear two hearts apart.<br /><br />I have been listening to one of Joshua Radin’s songs “When I find you” which fits Timeless.<br /><br />“Oh I need you to know today<br />I’ll wait for you always.<br />Oh I need you to know today<br />I’ll wait for you always.<br />Coz when I find you<br />I’ll find me”<br /><br />This book is totally a 5! I hope the next book gets released soon.<br />. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1323331237249802538" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_997263489" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/997263489" />
    <a title="Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd"><img alt="Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1382576238p2/8096484.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/997263489?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)" href="/user/show/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd">Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780385738392" href="/book/show/11783915-timeless">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=pov-girl">pov-girl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=penguin-random-house">penguin-random-house</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=insta-love">insta-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=covers-blueness">covers-blueness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=series-books">series-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=debuts">debuts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=books-bought-in-2017">books-bought-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=i-give-up">i-give-up</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer997263489" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1129074553611374971">This and other reviews can be found on <a href='http://thepsychoticnerd.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Psychotic Nerd</a><br/><br/><b>Actual Rating: 2.5 Stars</b><br/><br/><b>
  <u>MY THOUGHTS</u>
</b><br/>I am inbetween about my feelings on this book. On one hand, I am very disappointed. On the other, I actually sort of liked this book.<br/><br/>Starting this book, I was worried. This book immediately starting following what I can YA Book Syndrome. Two side effects of YA Book Syndrome is that our main character (usually a girl) faces a tragedy and/or moves to a new school (usually a private or boarding school). </span>
  <span id="freeText1129074553611374971" style="display:none">This and other reviews can be found on <a href="http://thepsychoticnerd.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Psychotic Nerd</a><br /><br /><b>Actual Rating: 2.5 Stars</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>MY THOUGHTS</u>
</b><br />I am inbetween about my feelings on this book. On one hand, I am very disappointed. On the other, I actually sort of liked this book.<br /><br />Starting this book, I was worried. This book immediately starting following what I can YA Book Syndrome. Two side effects of YA Book Syndrome is that our main character (usually a girl) faces a tragedy and/or moves to a new school (usually a private or boarding school). This book follows both of these "side effects" and it made me worry that this book was going to be just like every other YA book.<br />I honestly didn't have to worry about this. Sure, this book isn't completely original, but none of this is what disappointed me.<br /><br />I could not stand the romance.<br />I was actually fine with everything else, but whenever the romance took center stage, my opinion on the book went down. This book featured my least favorite type of romance: insta-love. Michele and Philip have an immediate attraction towards each other. It was cheesy and unbelievable. Maybe I could understand Michele, since she's had dreams about Philip her whole life, but Philip? I honestly couldn't believe it. This guy has never talked to her before (he did see her for a very brief moment), he's even engaged to someone, but he's willing to be with this girl for his life. I just honestly couldn't understand this instant attraction to one another.<br />Whenever the romance was in the book, which was maybe the middle portion of the book, I was very annoyed at the book, but the romance wasn't always the focus of the book. Obviously, there is time travel and time travel happens to be one of my favorite things that I can find in books. There are times when Michele goes back in time without going to see Philip and I loved those moments! I loved seeing the lives of the past! That's one of the reasons that I love time travel so much! And while I don't quite understand how it works, I do like the concept in the book.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>IN CONCLUSION</u>
</b><br />The romance was annoying and cliche, but the time travel was amazing!<br />If it wasn't for the romance, this book would have such a higher rating, but I just can't ignore the stupid romance. <br />As far as reading the sequel, I'm not sure. I am interested in continuing, as I want some more answers.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Why can Philip see her? What do her dreams mean? And what about her father? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And this book ends in a bit of a cliffhanger (Although, I don't care because it's a cliffhanger used way too often and it also involves Philip). But the next book isn't at my library and I don't really feel inclined to buy it. I'll guess I'll have to see.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1129074553611374971" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer154471513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12262679197558619209">hmmm how do I start.... this book was ok. I liked the whole time travel aspect of the book but that's about it. First I would like to say that the history and description of old New York was well done without being boring and the songs mentioned throughout the story I did look up and enjoyed. That being said the author lacked tact and finesse in her writing. For a good portion of the book the dialogue between the characters was kind of awkward as Monir tried to explain what was going on for the </span>
  <span id="freeText12262679197558619209" style="display:none">hmmm how do I start.... this book was ok. I liked the whole time travel aspect of the book but that's about it. First I would like to say that the history and description of old New York was well done without being boring and the songs mentioned throughout the story I did look up and enjoyed. That being said the author lacked tact and finesse in her writing. For a good portion of the book the dialogue between the characters was kind of awkward as Monir tried to explain what was going on for the readers to understand and the characters but she didn't pull it off at all. <br /><br />Another thing I found bothersome was the romance. I absolutely hate when the protagonists fall in love out of no where. I cannot stand a book where the romance in the story is not believable (I mean at least have a full conversation before you drop L word) and unfortunately this book was the quintessential example of what I dislike. That might have even be forgiven if the characters were likable. They weren't annoying just bland. I didn't see what it was about Phillip that michele liked so much besides the fact that he was good looking. It also bothered me how easily michele and her friend accepted the fact that she was time traveling. I mean wouldn't a normal person be a little freaked out and would want to figure out how it was he or she was doing it. In all there was as extreme lack of character development which therefore led to a lack of connection with the characters. I might give the second book a try if I have nothing to read (the ending did spike my curiosity a little) but I wouldn't hold my breathe.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12262679197558619209" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156467626" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9070945515748553632">I have found that it takes a really amazing writer to to justice to the "time travel"genre, there is just a certain finesse needed to do it right. Which is why when done well it is one of my favourite genres but when it isn't, it really falls flat. This book just came across as juvenile. I realise it is for a young adult audience but somehow I feel the adult was lost along the way. The characters are severely under developed and unrealistic. The fact that not one of them seems anything but mildl</span>
  <span id="freeText9070945515748553632" style="display:none">I have found that it takes a really amazing writer to to justice to the "time travel"genre, there is just a certain finesse needed to do it right. Which is why when done well it is one of my favourite genres but when it isn't, it really falls flat. This book just came across as juvenile. I realise it is for a young adult audience but somehow I feel the adult was lost along the way. The characters are severely under developed and unrealistic. The fact that not one of them seems anything but mildly surprised that Michele is jumping through time or is invisible seems a little strange to me.<br />These one dimensional character are extremely hard to connect with on any level. I will admit the the author did do some good work describing the roaring 20's and the music throughout, but I wish she had put as much passion into the love story. I have eaten dry toast that was less bland! There is no evidence of any real connection between the two main characters. All their dialogue and encounters seem stilted and uncomfortable and as far as I can tell the only thing Philip had going for him was his looks. Honestly If I were Michele I wouldn't bother travelling down the road to save such a stale relationship let alone through time. And please don't even get me started on the patched together ending!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9070945515748553632" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

I can’t put this book into words it was just so incredible. Imagine being able to time travel. *sigh*<br /><br />Michele has been having dreams about this boy that has the most beautiful sapphire eyes. She is attracted to him, but never saw him in her entire life. In the same dreams she has been having since she was a little kid.<br /> <br />This book was filled with so many twists and mystery, I couldn’t keep my eyes from flying over every word, soaking it all it. Let’s start at the beginning. <br /><br />Michele and her mom are like best friends, there very close. One day at school a police officer arrives at her school telling her the most tragic words she could ever hear. Her mom was in a car accident and is dead. Michele was devastated. She was an orphan. Her dad was never part of her life because her grandparents hated him. So her mom tells her. <br /><br />In the will the next guardians are her grandparents who she never met. She flies to New York and goes to live with her very wealthy grandparents. Her stuff was packed and sent to the new house (mansion) that she is now living in. She finds an unfamiliar box that holds her moms stuff. The stuff she held in a safe in a bank. In the box of stuff she finds a key. <br /><br />The key seems to be moving. She founds out the key opens up the locked drawer on the bottom of her desk. It opens up to be one of her ancestor’s diaries. It opens up and she is immediately sucked into the diary. She is in the year 1910. There she sees Philip Walker, the boy from her dreams. They lock eyes and both of them recognize each other but have never seen each other before.<br /><br />This book tells a story of Michele’s romance with a boy from the past and unraveling the mystery of who her dad really is. <br />The book ended so dumb. It was such a cliffhanger and I hope that I can travel to the future to receive the second book. The time keeper, which comes out in 2012<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14390978996375459494" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_146593008" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/146593008" />
    <a title="Keary Taylor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3701804-keary-taylor"><img alt="Keary Taylor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442513192p2/3701804.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/146593008?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keary Taylor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keary Taylor" href="/user/show/3701804-keary-taylor">Keary Taylor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer146593008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6234447935214361516">I had some really high expectations for Timeless. The description alone made me buy the book and the cover is lovely. I don’t normally get into historical romance or time travel stuff but for some reason I just really wanted to read this. <br/><br/>As I started reading it I actually looked up reviews on it. They were pretty much all really good. Everyone loved it and fell in love with the story.<br/><br/>I’m sad to say that I didn’t quite feel the same as everyone else. I’ll break it down for you in the good and th</span>
  <span id="freeText6234447935214361516" style="display:none">I had some really high expectations for Timeless. The description alone made me buy the book and the cover is lovely. I don’t normally get into historical romance or time travel stuff but for some reason I just really wanted to read this. <br /><br />As I started reading it I actually looked up reviews on it. They were pretty much all really good. Everyone loved it and fell in love with the story.<br /><br />I’m sad to say that I didn’t quite feel the same as everyone else. I’ll break it down for you in the good and the bad.<br /><br />First the bad: The biggest thing for me was the actual writing. It felt very awkward and unbelievable at times to me. It kind of felt like it was being written by a fourteen year old. And my other major problem with it was the characters. I didn’t feel a connection with any of them really, especially Phillip, the main guy in the romance. They just felt kinda… flat.<br /><br />Now the good: I do think Alexandra did a great job at describing historic New York. I’ve never been to New York so I had no idea what this world would look like so I though she did a fantastic job of painting the picture. I could picture the Windsor mansion and it felt like I was there. The author really did her research. And this story was actually wonderfully layered, toward the end. As Michele time travels you see different generations of her family, where people fit in in the overall story, and it actually turned out really well.<br /><br />Overall, I REALLY wanted to love this story. And the actual story was pretty good, the writing just didn’t quite live up to what I hoped it would be.<br /><br />2.5/5 stars<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6234447935214361516" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2251408985?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Morgan Bowser" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Morgan Bowser" href="/user/show/75911248-morgan-bowser">Morgan Bowser</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2251408985" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1190605755070768504">This is a classic case of why you should not judge a book by its cover. The cover is beautiful and the synopsis is interesting but this is a terrible book. I actually bought the 1st and 2nd book at the same time and I can't even force myself to read the second one with the crappiness of the first one burned into my brain. I only finished the first book out of sheer willpower.<br/><br/>**I should say though that I'm older than the target audience so that absolutely contributed to me hating this book.**<br/><br/>Wher</span>
  <span id="freeText1190605755070768504" style="display:none">This is a classic case of why you should not judge a book by its cover. The cover is beautiful and the synopsis is interesting but this is a terrible book. I actually bought the 1st and 2nd book at the same time and I can't even force myself to read the second one with the crappiness of the first one burned into my brain. I only finished the first book out of sheer willpower.<br /><br />**I should say though that I'm older than the target audience so that absolutely contributed to me hating this book.**<br /><br />Where to start...what isn't wrong with this book? The main character is ridiculous. Like, are real teens actually like her? I don't know, maybe it's Canada or a middle class thing but I was as mature as this character is when I was 10. <br /><br />There is literally no plot. "Oh I saw this guy in my dreams and he's hot, let's talk about that for awhile". <br /><br />The author attempts to have time travel-y things happen with absolutely no rhyme or reason or, heaven forbid, an explanation that makes sense. "But how can you travel back in time?" "I don't f*cking know, just forget about it"<br /><br />Honestly, I could go on but this book isn't even worth it.</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer205374711175049846">It shocks me that I loved this book immensely but never managed to write a review for this book until now. The reason, I was at loss of words. I didn't know how to express myself when it came to this book. Have you ever loved a book so much from the very first line you read. That's how much I liked this one. The story was original and captivating. The whole time travel thing was thoroughly entertaining and was kind of a change from the usual brand of unrequited love stories. And things had this </span>
  <span id="freeText205374711175049846" style="display:none">It shocks me that I loved this book immensely but never managed to write a review for this book until now. The reason, I was at loss of words. I didn't know how to express myself when it came to this book. Have you ever loved a book so much from the very first line you read. That's how much I liked this one. The story was original and captivating. The whole time travel thing was thoroughly entertaining and was kind of a change from the usual brand of unrequited love stories. And things had this uncanny ability of falling in to place and making perfect sense. But the end was as confusing as ever. Just when I decided that I could live with the kind of love story it shaped up to be the author went and threw a curve ball in my direction which had me running in loops. What the hell happened?? that was the question going over and over in mind again and again after finishing the story. Is it even possible?? After mussing over the problem for a couple of days I decided that somethings are better left alone and decided to wait patiently for the next book in the series. Hoping I don't have to wait too long</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2kU7BFk8eBhxpS8tsHSbLZeTJ4aGon3SgiWPXK68NC0MbdAWsYbjcC99Dz8fGTaY52WZlwMm+oGLQJ0nEUrD8w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OScxvV6Py9xD3H2gR9hpv8ZTnnNmW9bpeq1pMU6wrjvvD9qvtjVQtB0EXbLotcQKtqUgYuPfUbpzyHtK8UZZ5Q==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3505204.Alexandra_Monir">About Alexandra Monir</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3505204.Alexandra_Monir"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1509031586p3/3505204.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3403919359922078903">Alexandra Monir, Iranian-American author and recording artist, has published five novels for young adults, including her popular debut, Timeless. A Barnes & Noble best-seller and one of Amazon’s “Best Books of the Month,” Timeless and its sequel, Timekeeper, have been featured in numerous media outlets and been published in different countries around the world. She followed the duology with Suspic</span>
  <span id="freeText3403919359922078903" style="display:none">Alexandra Monir, Iranian-American author and recording artist, has published five novels for young adults, including her popular debut, Timeless. A Barnes &amp; Noble best-seller and one of Amazon’s “Best Books of the Month,” Timeless and its sequel, Timekeeper, have been featured in numerous media outlets and been published in different countries around the world. She followed the duology with Suspicion and The Girl in the Picture, both standalone YA thrillers. Her upcoming science fiction novel, THE FINAL SIX (March 6, 2018) was acquired by HarperCollins and Sony Pictures during the same week, in two major pre-emptive deals.<br /><br />Alexandra is also a singer/songwriter who often integrates music into her books’ pages. She wrote and recorded three original songs to accompany Timeless and Timekeeper, which were released as the album “The Timeless EP” and distributed by Jimmy Buffett’s record label, Mailboat Records. She also recorded a song that was released with the publication of Suspicion, and is composing a stage musical geared toward Broadway. Her musical roots are deep, as she is the granddaughter of the late Monir Vakili, the foremost Iranian opera singer.<br /><br />Alexandra Monir is a frequent speaker at middle schools and high schools across the country, and at major events including fan conventions, women’s leadership conferences, and book festivals. She is a member of the Iranian American Women Foundation, an organization near to her heart. Alexandra currently lives in Los Angeles with her husband and newborn son. To learn more about Alexandra, visit her online at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.alexandramonir.com">www.alexandramonir.com</a>.<br /><br />---<br /><br />AUTHOR LINKS:<br /><br />Facebook: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/AlexandraMonirAuthor">https://www.facebook.com/AlexandraMon...</a><br /><br />Twitter: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.twitter.com/TimelessAlex">https://www.twitter.com/TimelessAlex</a><br /><br />Instagram: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.instagram.com/AlexandraMonir">https://www.instagram.com/AlexandraMonir</a></span>
